# Investigation: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

**Repository:** grafana/grafana
**Task Type:** Regression Hunt (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After upgrading Grafana from v10.3 to v10.4, some dashboards with table panels fail to render correctly. The table panel's field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import. Users see tables with missing column formatting (column widths, text alignment, cell display modes).

The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON. Dashboards with explicit custom config render correctly.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Which migration function is responsible for the regression
2. The exact conditional logic that fails for dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`
3. Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected
4. Which dashboard schema version triggers the issue
5. The files and functions involved in the migration chain

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on the dashboard migration pipeline, particularly schema version handlers

     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering

    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)

    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality

Now I have a clear picture. Let me verify the local file to confirm the critical bug. The local code shows:

**Lines 115-123 of `v38.go`:**
```go
defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue  // <-- SKIPS ENTIRE PANEL including overrides!
}

custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue  // <-- SKIPS ENTIRE PANEL including overrides!
}
```

This is the bug. When `defaults["custom"]` doesn't exist (i.e., no explicit `custom` object in the dashboard JSON), the `continue` on line 122 **skips the entire panel** — including the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135.

This confirms the bug. On line 120-123, when `defaults["custom"]` doesn't exist as a `map[string]interface{}`, the code hits `continue` and **skips the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135**. This means field overrides containing `custom.displayMode` are never converted to `custom.cellOptions`.

Now let me compare with the frontend. In the frontend (`DashboardMigrator.ts:647-670`):

```typescript
if (panel.type === 'table' && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined) {
  const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;
  
  // Update field configuration (defaults)
  if (displayMode !== undefined) {
    panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayMode);
    delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.displayMode;
  }

  // Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode
  // THIS RUNS REGARDLESS of whether defaults.custom exists!
  if (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {
    for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) {
      ...
    }
  }
}
```

The frontend uses `?.` (optional chaining) to safely read `defaults?.custom?.displayMode`, so if `custom` doesn't exist, `displayMode` is simply `undefined` and the defaults block is skipped — but the overrides block **still executes**.

Now let me also check the test to see if it covers this case. Looking at the test file line 443-600, the second test case "table with missing defaults.custom but overrides with custom.displayMode" actually tests this exact scenario and expects the overrides to be migrated even when `defaults.custom` is absent.

Let me run the test to confirm the failure:

`applyPanelDefaults` does **not** add `defaults.custom`. It only ensures `fieldConfig`, `defaults`, and `overrides` exist, but never creates a `custom` sub-object. This confirms the root cause:

1. Dashboard JSON without `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` gets loaded
2. `applyPanelDefaults` ensures `fieldConfig.defaults` exists as `{}` but does **not** add `custom`
3. V38 migration runs, hits `defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})` which fails since `custom` doesn't exist
4. The `continue` skips the **entire panel**, including `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` on line 135
5. Field overrides with `custom.displayMode` remain unconverted → table columns lose their formatting

90-assistanttext-
The investigation is complete. Here's a summary of the findings:

**Root Cause:** In `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:120-122`, the `processPanelsV38` function performs a type assertion on `defaults["custom"]` and issues a `continue` when it fails. This `continue` skips the entire remaining loop body, including the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135. Consequently, any table panel without an explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object has its field overrides (containing `custom.displayMode` properties) silently left unconverted.

**Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` work:** The type assertion on line 120 succeeds, so execution falls through to both the defaults migration (lines 125-132) and the override migration (line 135).

**Frontend comparison:** The frontend `DashboardMigrator.ts` uses JavaScript optional chaining (`defaults?.custom?.displayMode`) and runs the override migration as an independent code block, not gated by the `defaults.custom` check.

**Schema version:** 38 — affects any dashboard with `schemaVersion` < 38 that has table panels with override-only column formatting.

The full report is at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

The original format\n11: // used string references that could break when datasources were renamed, moved between organizations,\n12: // or when multiple datasources shared similar names. This created reliability and portability issues\n13: // for dashboard sharing and automation workflows.\n14: //\n15: // The migration works by:\n16: // 1. Processing annotations, template variables, and panels (including nested panels in rows)\n17: // 2. Converting string datasource references to structured objects containing uid, type, and apiVersion\n18: // 3. Handling null/missing datasource references by setting appropriate defaults\n19: // 4. Maintaining consistency between panel and target datasource configurations\n20: // 5. Preserving special datasource types like Mixed datasources and expression queries\n21: //\n22: // This transformation provides several critical benefits:\n23: // - Eliminates datasource reference breakage when datasources are renamed\n24: // - Enables reliable dashboard export/import across different Grafana instances\n25: // - Supports advanced datasource features that require type and version information\n26: // - Prepares the schema for future datasource management enhancements\n27: // - Maintains backward compatibility while establishing a robust foundation\n28: //\n29: // The migration handles complex scenarios including:\n30: // - Panels with missing datasource configuration (set to default)\n31: // - Mixed datasource panels with heterogeneous targets\n32: // - Expression {
  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nThe V38 schema migration (`processPanelsV38` in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`) contains a control-flow bug where a `continue` statement on line 122 causes the entire panel processing loop body \u2014 including field override migration \u2014 to be skipped when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not explicitly set in the dashboard JSON. This means `custom.displayMode` override properties are never converted to `custom.cellOptions`, silently dropping column-level formatting (widths, alignment, cell display modes) on import.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n**Function:** `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)\n**Schema version trigger:** 38 (dashboards with `schemaVersion` < 38 trigger this migration)\n\nThe bug is in lines 115-123 of `v38.go`:\n\n```go\ndefaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue   // line 117 \u2014 skips panel if \"defaults\" is missing\n}\n\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue   // line 122 \u2014 BUG: skips panel INCLUDING override migration\n}\n```\n\nThe `continue` on line 122 is reached when `defaults[\"custom\"]` is absent or not a `map[string]interface{}`. Because `continue` jumps to the next loop iteration, the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135 is **never executed** for that panel.\n\n**Contrast with the frontend (correct behavior):**\n\nIn `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts` (lines 645-671), the equivalent migration uses JavaScript optional chaining:\n\n```typescript\nconst displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;\nif (displayMode !== undefined) {\n    // migrate defaults.custom only\n}\n// Override migration runs UNCONDITIONALLY here:\nif (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n    for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) { ... }\n}\n```\n\nIn the frontend, the defaults migration and override migration are **independent code blocks**. The absence of `defaults.custom` only causes the defaults block to be skipped; the override migration always runs. The backend Go code conflates both operations inside a single guarded block, causing the override path to be gated by the defaults check.\n\n## Evidence\n\n1. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:115-135`** \u2014 The `defaults[\"custom\"]` type assertion on line 120 gates both the defaults migration (lines 125-132) AND the override migration (line 135). When the assertion fails, `continue` on line 122 skips `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)`.\n\n2. **`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts:645-671`** \u2014 The frontend equivalent uses optional chaining (`defaults?.custom?.displayMode`) and runs override migration unconditionally at lines 660-669, independent of whether `defaults.custom` exists.\n\n3. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:75-126`** (`applyPanelDefaults`) \u2014 The backend pre-migration defaults function ensures `fieldConfig.defaults` and `fieldConfig.overrides` exist but does **not** create a `defaults.custom` object. This means any dashboard JSON that omits `custom` from `fieldConfig.defaults` will still have no `custom` key when V38 runs.\n\n4. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:1113-1132`** (`trackPanelOriginalFieldConfigCustom`) \u2014 Tracking of `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` only sets the marker when `defaults[\"custom\"]` exists in the original input. Dashboards without `custom` are never marked, so the cleanup path cannot restore anything.\n\n5. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`** \u2014 The local test file only contains one test case (\"table migration with nested panels\") which always includes explicit `defaults.custom`. The test case for \"table with missing defaults.custom but overrides with custom.displayMode\" is absent from the local codebase (present in later Sourcegraph-indexed revision at lines 443-603), confirming the bug was introduced with incomplete test coverage.\n\n6. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go:91`** \u2014 V38 is registered at schema version 38 in the migration map, confirming this is the migration that runs for dashboards upgrading past schema version 37.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`** \u2014 The migration function with the bug\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`** \u2014 Missing test coverage for the no-`defaults.custom` case\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go`** \u2014 Migration orchestrator that calls V38 (not buggy itself but is the entry point)\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`** \u2014 `applyPanelDefaults` correctly does not add `custom`, but this means V38 must handle its absence\n- **`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`** \u2014 Frontend reference implementation (correct behavior)\n- **Any table panel dashboard with `schemaVersion` < 38** that uses field overrides for column formatting (e.g., `custom.displayMode` in overrides) but does not have an explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object\n\n## Recommendation\n\nRestructure `processPanelsV38` to decouple the defaults migration from the override migration. The `defaults[\"custom\"]` check should only guard the defaults-specific code, not the entire panel. The override migration (`migrateOverrides`) must be called unconditionally for all table panels that have a valid `fieldConfig`, matching the frontend behavior.\n\nSpecifically, lines 115-135 should be restructured from:\n\n```go\ndefaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok { continue }\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok { continue }   // <-- skips overrides too\n\n// ... migrate defaults.custom ...\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n```\n\nTo:\n\n```go\n// Process defaults.custom if it exists\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        if displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n            if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n                custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n            }\n            delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// Update overrides REGARDLESS of whether defaults.custom exists\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n```\n\nAdditionally, the test file should include a test case for table panels where `fieldConfig.defaults` has no `custom` key but overrides contain `custom.displayMode` properties.\n",

        Code Changes (1)
        
1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report

## Summary

The V38 schema migration (`processPanelsV38` in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`) contains a control-flow bug where a `continue` statement on line 122 causes the entire panel processing loop body — including field override migration — to be skipped when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not explicitly set in the dashboard JSON. This means `custom.displayMode` override properties are never converted to `custom.cellOptions`, silently dropping column-level formatting (widths, alignment, cell display modes) on import.

## Root Cause

**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`
**Function:** `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)
**Schema version trigger:** 38 (dashboards with `schemaVersion` < 38 trigger this migration)

The bug is in lines 115-123 of `v38.go`:

```go
defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue   // line 117 — skips panel if "defaults" is missing
}

custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue   // line 122 — BUG: skips panel INCLUDING override migration
}
```

The `continue` on line 122 is reached when `defaults["custom"]` is absent or not a `map[string]interface{}`. Because `continue` jumps to the next loop iteration, the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135 is **never executed** for that panel.

**Contrast with the frontend (correct behavior):**

In `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts` (lines 645-671), the equivalent migration uses JavaScript optional chaining:

```typescript
const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;
if (displayMode !== undefined) {
    // migrate defaults.custom only
}
// Override migration runs UNCONDITIONALLY here:
if (panel.fieldCo
